    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

<span id="freeTextContainer16785057187500992221"><u>5 STAR'S</u> <br/><br/><b>
  <i>“If you can learn to endure pain, you can survive anything."</i>
</b><br/><br/><i>The Assassin and the Desert</i> was by far the best novella in this series thus far :) It takes place in The Red Desert with The Silent Assassins. Where Celeana was sent by Arobynn as punishment to train with The Mute Master. I thoroughly enjoyed every last minute of it!! It blew me away and I can't believe how much I truly loved it! I was very much surprised at all the twists and turns and the number of details <i>Maas</i> was able t</span>
  <span id="freeText16785057187500992221" style="display:none"><u>5 STAR'S</u> <br><br><b>
  <i>“If you can learn to endure pain, you can survive anything."</i>
</b><br><br><i>The Assassin and the Desert</i> was by far the best novella in this series thus far :) It takes place in The Red Desert with The Silent Assassins. Where Celeana was sent by Arobynn as punishment to train with The Mute Master. I thoroughly enjoyed every last minute of it!! It blew me away and I can't believe how much I truly loved it! I was very much surprised at all the twists and turns and the number of details <i>Maas</i> was able to fit into a 103-page novella. I was extremely happy that this one was longer and yet I still wanted more. Needed more. Yes, it was slow in parts but really for once, I didn't mind that fact at all. I enjoyed all the new characters I was introduced too. I loved seeing how Celeana and Ansel officially met and I love the friendship that bloomed between them. I was so sad about how everything went down at the end :( and in spite of the betrayal, I can't help it... I still really like Ansel. Honestly, guys, this book was so worth the read. I recommend if you get the chance to read it DO! You won't be disappointed :D <i>The Assassin and the Underworld</i> here I come! <br> <br><b>
  <i>“Words could be just as deadly as steel.”</i>
</b><br><br><i>“One arrow, that had been her promise. But she'd also promised Ansel that she had twenty minutes to get out of range. Celaena had fired after twenty-one.”</i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1482013335ra/21477172.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>“I think you will leave a lasting imprint on Ansel's heart. You spared her life, and returned her father's sword. And maybe when she makes her next move to reclaim her title, she will remember the assassin from the North and the kindness you showed her, and try to leave fewer bodies in her wake.”</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer18083398115505969636">4.5★ Loved it!<br/><br/> —𝙨𝙥𝙞𝙧𝙞𝙩 𝙛𝙧𝙤𝙢 𝙩𝙝𝙚 𝙣𝙤𝙧𝙩𝙝, 𝙨𝙩𝙧𝙚𝙣𝙜𝙩𝙝 𝙛𝙧𝙤𝙢 𝙩𝙝𝙚 𝙨𝙤𝙪𝙩𝙝, 𝙨𝙥𝙚𝙚𝙙 𝙛𝙧𝙤𝙢 𝙩𝙝𝙚 𝙚𝙖𝙨𝙩 𝙖𝙣𝙙 𝙬𝙞𝙨𝙙𝙤𝙢 𝙛𝙧𝙤𝙢 𝙩𝙝𝙚 𝙬𝙚𝙨𝙩, . . .<br/><br/>Celaena has to go to the Mute Master as her punishment and return with his letter of approval about her obedience and behaviour. If she does not return with it, she'll have to pay back Arobynn Hamel as much as he spent on her.<br/><br/>What if going back with the letter is her only option?<br/>But what if new ways open for Celaena? <br/><br/>“𝙏𝙤 𝙢𝙖𝙠𝙞𝙣𝙜 𝙖𝙢𝙚𝙣𝙙𝙨—𝙖𝙣𝙙 𝙛𝙤𝙣𝙙 𝙢𝙚𝙢𝙤𝙧𝙞𝙚𝙨.” “𝙏𝙤 𝙗𝙚𝙞𝙣𝙜 𝙩𝙝𝙚 𝙢𝙤𝙨𝙩 𝙛𝙚𝙖𝙧𝙨𝙤𝙢𝙚 </span>
  <span id="freeText18083398115505969636" style="display:none">4.5★ Loved it!<br><br> —𝙨𝙥𝙞𝙧𝙞𝙩 𝙛𝙧𝙤𝙢 𝙩𝙝𝙚 𝙣𝙤𝙧𝙩𝙝, 𝙨𝙩𝙧𝙚𝙣𝙜𝙩𝙝 𝙛𝙧𝙤𝙢 𝙩𝙝𝙚 𝙨𝙤𝙪𝙩𝙝, 𝙨𝙥𝙚𝙚𝙙 𝙛𝙧𝙤𝙢 𝙩𝙝𝙚 𝙚𝙖𝙨𝙩 𝙖𝙣𝙙 𝙬𝙞𝙨𝙙𝙤𝙢 𝙛𝙧𝙤𝙢 𝙩𝙝𝙚 𝙬𝙚𝙨𝙩, . . .<br><br>Celaena has to go to the Mute Master as her punishment and return with his letter of approval about her obedience and behaviour. If she does not return with it, she'll have to pay back Arobynn Hamel as much as he spent on her.<br><br>What if going back with the letter is her only option?<br>But what if new ways open for Celaena? <br><br>“𝙏𝙤 𝙢𝙖𝙠𝙞𝙣𝙜 𝙖𝙢𝙚𝙣𝙙𝙨—𝙖𝙣𝙙 𝙛𝙤𝙣𝙙 𝙢𝙚𝙢𝙤𝙧𝙞𝙚𝙨.” “𝙏𝙤 𝙗𝙚𝙞𝙣𝙜 𝙩𝙝𝙚 𝙢𝙤𝙨𝙩 𝙛𝙚𝙖𝙧𝙨𝙤𝙢𝙚 𝙖𝙣𝙙 𝙞𝙢𝙥𝙤𝙨𝙞𝙣𝙜 𝙜𝙞𝙧𝙡𝙨 𝙩𝙝𝙚 𝙬𝙤𝙧𝙡𝙙 𝙝𝙖𝙨 𝙚𝙫𝙚𝙧 𝙨𝙚𝙚𝙣.”<br><br>Celaena has never had any friends, but it seems like she has one now. But can she trust her? I bet you'll trust her as you read. I trusted her too! <br><br>𝙄𝙛 𝙮𝙤𝙪 𝙘𝙖𝙣 𝙡𝙚𝙖𝙧𝙣 𝙩𝙤 𝙚𝙣𝙙𝙪𝙧𝙚 𝙥𝙖𝙞𝙣, 𝙮𝙤𝙪 𝙘𝙖𝙣 𝙨𝙪𝙧𝙫𝙞𝙫𝙚 𝙖𝙣𝙮𝙩𝙝𝙞𝙣𝙜. 𝙎𝙤𝙢𝙚 𝙥𝙚𝙤𝙥𝙡𝙚 𝙡𝙚𝙖𝙧𝙣 𝙩𝙤 𝙚𝙢𝙗𝙧𝙖𝙘𝙚 𝙞𝙩—𝙩𝙤 𝙡𝙤𝙫𝙚 𝙞𝙩. 𝙎𝙤𝙢𝙚 𝙚𝙣𝙙𝙪𝙧𝙚 𝙞𝙩 𝙩𝙝𝙧𝙤𝙪𝙜𝙝 𝙙𝙧𝙤𝙬𝙣𝙞𝙣𝙜 𝙞𝙩 𝙞𝙣 𝙨𝙤𝙧𝙧𝙤𝙬, 𝙤𝙧 𝙗𝙮 𝙢𝙖𝙠𝙞𝙣𝙜 𝙩𝙝𝙚𝙢𝙨𝙚𝙡𝙫𝙚𝙨 𝙛𝙤𝙧𝙜𝙚𝙩. 𝙊𝙩𝙝𝙚𝙧𝙨 𝙩𝙪𝙧𝙣 𝙞𝙩 𝙞𝙣𝙩𝙤 𝙖𝙣𝙜𝙚𝙧.<br><br>While living with the Mute Master's silent assassins, Celaena feels a belonging. She starts to care about them, and when she has to leave, with or without the letter of approval, she has to make a choice. And by making that choice, she has no idea what her future might hold.<br><br>I must say, the writing style has been improved a lot!! Sometimes, you didn't even have to imagine. It was like everything happening in front of you.<br><br>— I was reading my own review and thinking is this the same author who wrote acotar books? Because I HATED the writing in those. And even in some tog books.😔💔<br><br>‼️ <b>SPOILER ALERT</b> ‼️<br><br>Also, I just saw this fanart and I HAD TO EDIT to add it to me review.<br><br>I loved the scene where Ansel and Celaena stole the horses. That was beautiful and so much fun. I LOVED IT!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1604826894i/30350719._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

    <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell"><img alt="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584062476p2/2190064.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2672630942?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell">Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=ya-ya-land">ya-ya-land</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2672630942" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15968413818297572186"><a href='http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/><br/><i>"You're just a spoiled, selfish bitch."</i><br/><br/><br/><br/>Celery's punishment saga continues as she finally makes her way into the Red Desert, a vaguely Middle Eastern land where the Silent Assassins live. The Silent Assassins seem to borrow <i>very </i>heavy from George R. R. Martin's Faceless Men, and it's almost funny how closely this story arc mirrors Arya's training under Jaqen H'ghar. But this is not the first thing in this series I've seen that really remi</span>
  <span id="freeText15968413818297572186" style="display:none"><a href="http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br><i>"You're just a spoiled, selfish bitch."</i><br><br><br><br>Celery's punishment saga continues as she finally makes her way into the Red Desert, a vaguely Middle Eastern land where the Silent Assassins live. The Silent Assassins seem to borrow <i>very </i>heavy from George R. R. Martin's Faceless Men, and it's almost funny how closely this story arc mirrors Arya's training under Jaqen H'ghar. But this is not the first thing in this series I've seen that really reminded me of Game of Thrones. The valg are <i>pretty </i>similar to the wights, Mannon and her wyvern is basically a knockoff Daenerys Targaryen (I mean, she's a dragon queen with white-blond hair), and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2447328703" rel="nofollow noopener">QUEEN OF SHADOWS</a> introduces something called "hellfire" that sounds a lot like wildfire. I'm not even a hardcore GoT fan, and even <i>I </i>noticed the similarities.<br><br><i> </i><br><br>Long story shorts, Celery must study under the Silent Assassins and get a letter of recommendation from them. While there, she makes friends with a girl named Ansel, who has a tragic history of her own. After her initial distrust with anything female, Celery finally condescends to accept these overtures of friendship and actually find herself quite taken with the chatty red-haired girl. Of <i>course</i>, this being a <i>Throne of Glass </i>novella, this comes to nothing.<br><br><br><br>Okay, seriously, what is the deal with the way women are treated in this book. Good women are chaste and end up married and pregnant by their mates, whereas bad women are slutty or power-hungry and ambitious. Even Celery, who's supposed to be the best of the best, doesn't actually do much that's bad-ass. Considering how all of these novellas have the words "assassin" in the title, she doesn't do much assassinating. In fact, she balks from it at every opportunity, even if it's her damn job. And <i>I'm sorry </i>but how does killing people of adultery weigh more than killing people who are essentially selling people (including youths) into prostitution (per pirate lord)? She should have killed Rolfe, but she didn't. And when Ansel betrays her in this book, because of course she does, nobody can eclipse our shining star, Celery Saltine-thin, Queen of Every Fucking Thing, Celery doesn't even kill <i>her</i>. She lets her get away with betraying all the people who took her in. <i>Because of course she does</i>. She even manages to get herself drugged/poisoned by quaffing food that's put in front of her.<br><br><br><br>Best. Assassin. <i>Ever</i>.<br><br><br><br>Despite my complaints, this is easily the best of the three assassin prequel novellas I've read so far. The scenery descriptions are much better here, and all of the side characters are interesting (except for, you know, <i>Celery</i>). The way Ansel was treated in this book was basically Nehemia pt. 2 and I don't know why Maas seems so reluctant to portray healthy female friendships, but man, it's becoming a pattern and it's kind of upsetting. Nehemia was the best part about books one and two, and we all know how that went down. Ansel was a repeat of that. Don't be friends with women, I guess, or they'll either try to kill you or die for your sins. Oh, and Celery adds <i>yet another conquest </i>to her ever-growing man-harem, the ill-fated assassin, Ilias. Honestly, considering how cruelly these books treat sexually empowered women, Celery sure has a lot of admirers.<br><br><br><br>2 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="15968413818297572186" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2285333230" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2285333230" />
    <a title="Isa Cantos (Crónicas de una Merodeadora)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20954985-isa-cantos-cr-nicas-de-una-merodeadora"><img alt="Isa Cantos (Crónicas de una Merodeadora)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594228529p2/20954985.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2285333230?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Isa Cantos (Crónicas de una Merodeadora)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Isa Cantos (Crónicas de una Merodeadora)" href="/user/show/20954985-isa-cantos-cr-nicas-de-una-merodeadora">Isa Cantos (Crónicas de una Merodeadora)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2285333230" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10075786240213894575"><i>
  <b>"The Lord of the North".<br/>"Why does he get a fancy title?"<br/>"Because the stag remains constant—no matter the season, he's always there".<br/>"Why?"<br/>"So the people of Terrasen will always know how to find their way home. So they can look up at the sky, no matter where they are, and know Terrasen is forever with them".</b>
</i><br/><br/>¡Este es uno de los mejores relatos del libro! La intriga, los viajes, los acertijos, el entrenamiento, las traiciones... <i>The Assassin and the Desert</i> lo tiene todo. Aquí, Celaena va a tene</span>
  <span id="freeText10075786240213894575" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>"The Lord of the North".<br />"Why does he get a fancy title?"<br />"Because the stag remains constant—no matter the season, he's always there".<br />"Why?"<br />"So the people of Terrasen will always know how to find their way home. So they can look up at the sky, no matter where they are, and know Terrasen is forever with them".</b>
</i><br /><br />¡Este es uno de los mejores relatos del libro! La intriga, los viajes, los acertijos, el entrenamiento, las traiciones... <i>The Assassin and the Desert</i> lo tiene todo. Aquí, Celaena va a tener que llegar a la guarida de los Asesinos Silenciosos, después de atravesar todo el Desierto Rojo, y convencer al gran Maestro de que la entrene durante un mes. Y no sólo eso, sino que también tendrá que lograr que el Maestro le escriba una carta de aprobación para que Arobynn perdone sus insolencias y la deje volver a Rifthold. Pronto, Celaena se da cuenta de que su misión no será nada fácil, pues un gran traición pende sobre la Fortaleza Silenciosa.<br /><br />En este relato nos encontramos con una faceta de Celaena que no conocíamos: la de alguien acostumbrada a ser la mejor y a sobresalir en todo pero que, de repente, se topa con personas y entrenamientos que rivalizan con sus habilidades y que, incluso, la superan. En la Fortaleza Silenciosa, Celaena aprende a ser un poco más humilde y a valorar las técnicas milenarias que les han dado su reputación a los Asesinos Silenciosos. Además, y paralelo a su entrenamiento, Celaena conocerá a Ansel, una chica letal que pronto se convertirá en algo parecido a su amiga... pero a qué precio. <br /><br />Me fascinó el ritmo que llevaba esta historia. Sarah J. Maas nos presenta un mundo alejado de Rifthold, del Gremio de los Asesinos y de la gran reputación de Celaena como la Asesina de Adarlan. El Desierto Rojo es un mundo completamente distinto, al igual que las alianzas, relaciones y traiciones políticas que se fraguan allí. Me gustó muchísimo conocer, finalmente, la épica historia del robo de los caballos Asterion al Lord de Xandria, que se menciona brevemente en <i>Crown of Midnight</i>. Ver cómo, poco a poco, pequeños detalles de estos relatos encajan en la gran historia de los libros principales es buenísimo. <br /><br />Ahora, cuando lean este relato, prepárense para los giros y las puñaladas por la espalda que incluye Sarah en esta historia porque, realmente, los van a dejar sin aire y sin ganas de confiar en absolutamente nadie a lo largo de su vida.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10075786240213894575" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1393081923?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pearl Angeli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pearl Angeli" href="/user/show/31514572-pearl-angeli">Pearl Angeli</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/13565653-the-assassin-and-the-desert">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=2015-reads">2015-reads</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1393081923" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11882264156674981250">Out of all the novellas of <b>The Assassin’s Blade</b> that I’ve read so far, this third novella is the best one. It’s action-packed and full of bad-assery! Celaena never fails to really impress me with the way she deals with her situations. After being punished by her master <b>Arrobyn</b>, she was instructed to travel to the <b>Deserted Lands</b> to train with the <b>master of the Silent Assassins</b>. There, she met people who became her friends, including the girl assassin <b>Ansel</b> who had a very painful and cruel childho</span>
  <span id="freeText11882264156674981250" style="display:none">Out of all the novellas of <b>The Assassin’s Blade</b> that I’ve read so far, this third novella is the best one. It’s action-packed and full of bad-assery! Celaena never fails to really impress me with the way she deals with her situations. After being punished by her master <b>Arrobyn</b>, she was instructed to travel to the <b>Deserted Lands</b> to train with the <b>master of the Silent Assassins</b>. There, she met people who became her friends, including the girl assassin <b>Ansel</b> who had a very painful and cruel childhood.<br /><br />The thing that I love most about <b>The Assassin and the Desert</b> is that it does not only have action scenes that will thrill you. It’s also meaningful. I love Celeana’s relationship with the master of the Silent Assassin. It tugged my heart in ways I did not expect. The way he taught her about life was so touching.<br /><br /> <i>
  <b>“If you can learn to endure pain, you can survive it.”</b>
</i> <br /><br />This novella made me smile and tearful. It’s something that I will not forget in this series. Plus, the setting was wonderfully described, painting captivating images of The Deserted Land. I think this is the best that I have read in the series so far, to be honest. What a journey!<br /><br />Rating: 5 Stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="11882264156674981250" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1780785042" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10740633800729123268">Finally I am getting around to reading the adventures of my dear Celaena Sardothien. <i>LOWKEY</i>, I kind of love the assassin more than the queen, but that <u>doesn't mean that I don't love the queen</u>. <br/><br/>I wanted to read it before I read Empire of Storms BUT I kind of got distracted with other books that were coming out around the same time. I am not a huge fan of novellas, but I do know that some of the characters introduced in the last book were first introduced in some of these novellas in <b>The Assassin'</b></span>
  <span id="freeText10740633800729123268" style="display:none">Finally I am getting around to reading the adventures of my dear Celaena Sardothien. <i>LOWKEY</i>, I kind of love the assassin more than the queen, but that <u>doesn't mean that I don't love the queen</u>. <br><br>I wanted to read it before I read Empire of Storms BUT I kind of got distracted with other books that were coming out around the same time. I am not a huge fan of novellas, but I do know that some of the characters introduced in the last book were first introduced in some of these novellas in <b>The Assassin's Blade</b>. And because I love <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3433047.Sarah_J_Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">Sarah J. Maas's</a>
</b> story telling and her writing, I am going to go ahead and read these beauties.<br><br>So, with that said, I am going to read and rate these so I can finally be completely caught up on The Throne of Glass Series: Throne of Glass, Crown of Midnight, Heir of Fire, Queen of Shadows, Empire of Storms, and Tower of Dawn.<br><br><u>The Assassin and the Desert (Throne of Glass, #0.3)</u><br>So this novella is also <b>one that needs to be read before you read Empire of Storms</b>, because it sheds a lot of light on certain characters that are going to be introduced.<br><br>Celaena and her actions from previous novella <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1780731874" rel="nofollow noopener">The Assassin and the Pirate Lord</a> have gotten her sent to <i>The Red Desert</i> with <b>The Silent Assassins</b>. She has to come back with a letter of approval basically from the Master of the Silent Assassins after training with him, only getting him to train you is actually super hard. <br><br><b>ENTER ANSEL:</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1512945653ra/24649388.gif" alt="" width="350" height="197" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>She meets <b>Ansel</b>, who is the lady introduced in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1740486622?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Empire of Storms</a>. She is basically Celaena in my opinion. They are both really proud of themselves and know they are hot stuff. They become really close friends in the month that Celaena is there. They even commit some crimes together, which is what true friendship is.<br><br>But there is someone who wants The Master of the Silent Assassins' head on a platter for them, and there is someone in the keep ready to take it in order to get what they want.<br><br>I liked this novella enough. I felt as if there were some filler paragraphs and I found myself yawning at some points, but it is a <u>very needed novella</u> if we are going to talk more about The Red Desert, The Silent Assassins, Ansel and even about the witches (because we get to learn more about them in this book too). <br><br>I want to feel spider-silk. That's all. </span>

<div id="review_952860052" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/952860052" />
    <a title="Kaya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15462098-kaya"><img alt="Kaya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485382914p2/15462098.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/952860052?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaya" href="/user/show/15462098-kaya">Kaya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer952860052" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5969454885252837130">I wonder what exactly was I supposed to learn about Celaena from this unnecessary novella when it only made me feel even less fond of her. Overall, nothing even slightly important happens, not for the series, and definitely not for our "beloved" protagonist. She shows off her complex of a higher value anywhere she goes, which is not particularly likable.<br/><br/>Celaena is being sent to the desert to train with The Silent Assassins in order to be taught about obedience and discipline. She hopes she'll be</span>
  <span id="freeText5969454885252837130" style="display:none">I wonder what exactly was I supposed to learn about Celaena from this unnecessary novella when it only made me feel even less fond of her. Overall, nothing even slightly important happens, not for the series, and definitely not for our "beloved" protagonist. She shows off her complex of a higher value anywhere she goes, which is not particularly likable.<br /><br />Celaena is being sent to the desert to train with The Silent Assassins in order to be taught about obedience and discipline. She hopes she'll be able to catch the attention of the Mute Master, whose letter of approval she must obtain in only one month. Despite the fact her roommate Ansel has been living there for five years and has received no private lessons whatsoever, Celaena, being as childish and insufferable as ever, throws little snarky comments how she should be getting more special attention because she's such a BIG BAD ASSASSIN. I've read FIVE books about her and I still don't see even a tiny notion about her actual skills. There is only telling and no showing and it's making me nauseous.<br /><br />The writing style is as simple as ever. It doesn't necessarily mean it's bad, but it lacks some lyrical or rather poetical elements, humor and generally some witty dialogues. Or maybe I'm just used to more developed characters and stories. The overall impression is simply... lazy like Maas wrote it in two hours.<br /><br />It seems almost impossible that I adored Celaena in Throne of Glass since she represents all the boring clichés of YA heroine. Again, she shows all shades of vanity, egotism, and arrogance. In addition, her reactions don't really show us the world-class assassin, only a 17-year-old attention whore. Probably the best quote in the whole series so far is Ansel's "You’re just a spoiled, selfish bitch.”</span>
  <a data-text-id="5969454885252837130" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10059031920559036831" style="display:none">.<blockquote>
  <b>"The Lord of the North".<br />"Why does he get a fancy title?"<br />"Because the stag remains constant—no matter the season, he's always there".<br />"Why?"<br />"So the people of Terrasen will always know how to find their way home. So they can look up at the sky, no matter where they are, and know Terrasen is forever with them"</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />This one was one of my favorite Novellas! Celaena ventures to the Red Dessert as punishment to train with the Silent Assassins. I adored the Mute Master and even though we dont really see much interaction between him and the assassins of his guild, you can still tell that he treats them properly. Unlike Arobynn.<br /><br />Celaena worked hard to get her letter of recommendation and met some new friends on the way. Most importantly, Ansel. I was intrigued by her story and I know that she comes in the later Throne of Glass books (which I haven’t reached just yet) so it should be interesting to see where life has brought her since then.<br /><br /> <br />|| <a href="https://theperksofbeingnourablog.wordpress.com/2018/05/23/the-assassin-and-the-desert-by-sarah-j-maas-mini-review/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> || <a href="https://www.instagram.com/theperksofbeingnoura/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> ||</span>

I really liked this story, and it actually is pretty thought provoking on the subject of abuse. Even though we are watching Celaena try to get a letter of recommendation for the Mute Master, we also get to see her inner struggle dealing with her own abusive master. Celaena is now seventeen and realizing all the abusive things that have happened in her life are not normal or okay. <br /><br />Celaena also befriends a young girl named Ansel, and I absolutely devoured her story-arc. Ansel is another character that I pray we get to see in this series eventually.   <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1884935097" />
    <a title="_racheljane_" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54315548-racheljane"><img alt="_racheljane_" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1469002514p2/54315548.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1884935097?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="_racheljane_" class="user" itemprop="url" name="_racheljane_" href="/user/show/54315548-racheljane">_racheljane_</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1884935097" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1116548296703896064">I really enjoyed the characters in this novella. It was refreshing to have a fresh set of characters to learn about. I loved Ansel and the dynamic she plays with Celaena. It’s interesting to see the difference in the two assassins’ and learn about how Ansel grew up. I also loved the Mute Master. He is kinder than Arrobyn Hamel and treats his assassins better than Arrobyn ever would. I liked that the Silent Assassins were more of a brotherhood and worked together.<br/><br/>The change of setting was refresh</span>
  <span id="freeText1116548296703896064" style="display:none">I really enjoyed the characters in this novella. It was refreshing to have a fresh set of characters to learn about. I loved Ansel and the dynamic she plays with Celaena. It’s interesting to see the difference in the two assassins’ and learn about how Ansel grew up. I also loved the Mute Master. He is kinder than Arrobyn Hamel and treats his assassins better than Arrobyn ever would. I liked that the Silent Assassins were more of a brotherhood and worked together.<br /><br />The change of setting was refreshing also. Instead of being in a town Celaena finds herself in the middle of the Red Desert with no one else but the Silent Assassins around for miles. I feel that the remote setting gives Celaena a chance to think for a while and better her skills.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1116548296703896064" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer999108337" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17781931765767798404">This is my favorite so far of the novellas that I've read. <br/><br/>But - and maybe this is just me - I feel a little set adrift in these prequels. I mean I know, logically, that they're leading to something, but I can't really see what exactly. And that's probably purposefully. Additionally, because of the assassin angle, I find myself not trusting anyone. It makes it a bit hard to form attachments to characters - other than Calaena that is. The side effect of that is that I'm forming a closer attachmen</span>
  <span id="freeText17781931765767798404" style="display:none">This is my favorite so far of the novellas that I've read. <br /><br />But - and maybe this is just me - I feel a little set adrift in these prequels. I mean I know, logically, that they're leading to something, but I can't really see what exactly. And that's probably purposefully. Additionally, because of the assassin angle, I find myself not trusting anyone. It makes it a bit hard to form attachments to characters - other than Calaena that is. The side effect of that is that I'm forming a closer attachment to Calaena. These novellas are supposed to be tantalizing, making me want to know more.<br /><br />They're succeeding. I'm interested in the world - in the magic (that's apparently no longer there), in the people, and the intrigues, and these moments with characters that we're meeting along the way. I find myself hoping that we'll get to see some of them again in the future.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17781931765767798404" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1890367488" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer13716540255446349737">Great origin story of how Aelin met Ansel. Recommend it for anyone about to read Empire of Storms!<br/><br/>I really love the southern twang that Ansel has in the audiobook :D</span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('JF6iZ5OLjvFOlE4tqRY/ScUKGJqOtX73lIzztB7RT6UaHpuHzAffzRfDpZ5+HwTeCTTOcY/YzGCx5xSvdEhAOQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('OeQKwkGkkVIzjPhh1TIfRdvvARkIbl5hj+I0STjwjmcHpDMiHijAbmrbE9ICOyTSF9HX8gkD7PaqidNSUmmB+w==')})
  }
